  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }

      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',

        state: 'apple_oauth_state_812f3619-eee1-44f9-a5eb-da7b32a5f3ed'
      });

<span id="freeTextContainer15366993190884587744">This is the last episode of Andrea Hirata. The rule to enjoy this book :<br/><br/>1. Stop make personification between Ikal and Andrea. They might be came from the same mind but the character and the flow of story could be different. I successfully avoided publisher's jargon before read it!<br/>2. Being a dreamer doesn't mean a fiction nor an illusion. <br/>3. For you who expect too much from this book, I think you should let the book tell itself. Just enjoy it, no matter what people say.<br/>4. If you just want the sto</span>
  <span id="freeText15366993190884587744" style="display:none">This is the last episode of Andrea Hirata. The rule to enjoy this book :<br /><br />1. Stop make personification between Ikal and Andrea. They might be came from the same mind but the character and the flow of story could be different. I successfully avoided publisher's jargon before read it!<br />2. Being a dreamer doesn't mean a fiction nor an illusion. <br />3. For you who expect too much from this book, I think you should let the book tell itself. Just enjoy it, no matter what people say.<br />4. If you just want the story literally, forget it. You will disappointed. Try to 'read' beyond the story. Such as : local wisdom and conservative values or the loves of history and nation's pride. You will find more than in the book if you can read it in different view.<br /><br />Overall : I love it!</span>

As the final book in Laskar Pelangi tetralogy, Maryamah Karpov gives me a sense of closure on the life of Ikal and his friends, family members and loved ones. The only thing that I detest is the cliffhanger ending where we are left wondering what will happen to Ikal and Aling. However, I couldn't ask for a better story that tugs at my heartstrings in every single chapter. Or should I say mozaik?</span>

<div id="review_648922056" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/648922056" />
    <a title="Andi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21522176-andi"><img alt="Andi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1590355963p2/21522176.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/648922056?book_show_action=true">Jun 23, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Andi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Andi" href="/user/show/21522176-andi">Andi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer648922056" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer11042655339972412212"><br/>In general, this novel tells the life Maryamah Karpov, Ikal after he successfully graduated from the Universite de Paris, Sorbonne, France. In the first chapter, the story opens with a scene examination Ikal thesis tested by famous lecturers are very ruthless in dealing with student exams. For those who are stuck thesis, the story at the beginning of this chapter will certainly enchant you. Moreover, the expertise of Andrea Hirata makes the story more fun to read.<br/><br/>After completing the test well, </span>
  <span id="freeText11042655339972412212" style="display:none"><br />In general, this novel tells the life Maryamah Karpov, Ikal after he successfully graduated from the Universite de Paris, Sorbonne, France. In the first chapter, the story opens with a scene examination Ikal thesis tested by famous lecturers are very ruthless in dealing with student exams. For those who are stuck thesis, the story at the beginning of this chapter will certainly enchant you. Moreover, the expertise of Andrea Hirata makes the story more fun to read.<br /><br />After completing the test well, Ikal retold to Indonesia with a number of French thought that a little contrary to what is happening in his hometown. At this gap, the author Andrea Hirata insert social criticism as Indonesia that left so as to underestimate the potential of the nation.<br /><br />The story in this novel continues as Karpov Maryamah, Ikal reunited with all of his friends in the village Arai and other members of the rainbow. The story so the blue. This novel also revolves around the relationship Ikal with his friends abroad and also the story of a long quest to find true love, A Ling. Firmly, hold Ikal vague trace A Ling. He was even willing to go to an island called rock only to find A Ling. Rock itself is famous as the island where the pirates hide from the authorities catch.<br /><br />If viewed from the language selection in the sentences, Andrea Hirata still using the old style that he used in the previous series novel. The story in the novel is as flowing Maryamah Karpov is. Although admittedly, there are many parts that seemed forced. Critics claim that although the work is fiction, but that does not mean its logical value should not be lost. Maryamah Karpov in the novel, there are some scenes that felt less realistic and fanciful impressed. For some people this is certainly disturbing. But for those others, fantasy is the very thing that makes the rainbow much loved readers.<br /><br />As a final conclusion, what is described in the synopsis Maryamah Karpov is only part of the story of the whole story. Andrea Hirata's novel, however, is a book to be read and collected serviceability. The story is inspiring and well in facing the nation's education better. Happy reading ya!</span>
  <a data-text-id="11042655339972412212" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <span id="freeText4640970700575549357" style="display:none">Maryamah Karpov is the fourth and final book of Laskar Pelangi tetralogy, written by Andrea Hirata. This novel is a continuation of the previous Edensor tells the story of Ikal travel Sourbone undergoing his education in France. Ikal was the son of a tin miner in Belitong, even though he was not the son of a wealthy family, but with the spirit and the dream he managed to get a scholarship to continue his master to Sourbone french. In part this novel tells Ikal has graduated from S2 and returned home to Belitong. After the departure of A Ling, Ikal has visited many places including places in the world only to find A Ling. Finally the sign of A Ling has appeared. He tried various ways to find A Ling, including making the ship to sail to find A Ling, assisted by his little friend Lintar a very intelligent, she finally managed to build ships. After several days he sailed through all the hurdles that exist, eventually struggle for years to find A Ling was not in vain. Ikal had found A Ling. But their love was full of sacrifices can not make Ikal and A Ling united, because Ikal's father did not approve them. For you lovers of the novel of course you are familiar with the novel Laskar Pelangi by Andrea Hirata, of course, you also have to read the last part of this novel. Written by recounting the life and culture of the people wither. This novel tells the struggle to achieve a dream. Although this novel does not end happily, but this novel is not to be missed to read, because the start of the first novel until the latter is really a story full of premises presents a moral message and give a lot of motivation.</span>

<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fC3/kjhCnzuaRtGh/X2O+GpemvcW62JWwclLfwFZ4dR9OphEn97KINzWGdmWAF/q/YbarNf3hIqHD7QWHCqkMg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('fnWnOHdqIR0/rN5VflYTtskeIckW9THGXsp8CGPx32J/YsDu0PZ0Bnk8Fi0VK8KkXsZhktfp1xoYDINhfoKahA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer8399626675267233011">Under a bright sunny sky, the three-day Byron Bay Writers’ Festival welcomed Andrea Hirata who charmed audiences with his modesty and gracious behavior during two sessions. <br/><br/>Andrea also attended a special event where he and Tim Baker, an Australian surfing writer, spoke to a gathering of several hundred school children. During one session, Andrea was on a panel with Pulitzer Prize winning journalis</span>
  <span id="freeText8399626675267233011" style="display:none">Under a bright sunny sky, the three-day Byron Bay Writers’ Festival welcomed Andrea Hirata who charmed audiences with his modesty and gracious behavior during two sessions. <br /><br />Andrea also attended a special event where he and Tim Baker, an Australian surfing writer, spoke to a gathering of several hundred school children. During one session, Andrea was on a panel with Pulitzer Prize winning journalist from Washington, DC, Katharine Boo, which he said was a great honor.<br /><br />The August event for the school children was very meaningful to Andrea, the barefooted boy from <br />Belitung, as he made mental comparisons with the educational opportunities of these children, compared to what he experienced. <br /><br />And now his own life story is about to become even more amazing, as his book Laskar Pelangi (The Rainbow Troops) is being published around the world in no less than twenty-four countries and in 12 languages. It has caught the eye of some of the world’s top publishing houses, such as Penguin, Random House, Farrar, Straus and Giroux, (New York, US) and many others. Translations are already on sale in Brazil, Taiwan, South Korea and Malaysia. <br /><br />All this has come about because of the feeling of appreciation that the young Andrea felt for his teacher, Muslimah. He promised her that he’d write a book for her someday. This was because for him and his school friends, a book was the most valuable thing they could think of. <br /><br />Andrea told a story that illustrated this fact. When royalties flowed in for him he decided to give his community a library. He spent a lot of money on books. He left the village headman in charge of administering the library. However, when he came back several months later, all the books were gone. People loved the books, but they had no concept of how a lending library functioned. <br /><br />“Some of them could not even read, but they just loved to have a book, an object of great value and importance, in their homes. We will restock the library with books and this time it will be run by our own administration,” he laughed.<br /><br />Andrea told this story as we sat in the coffee shop adjoining a Gold Coast City Library, one of 12 scattered around the city. One of the librarians, Jenneth Duque, showed him around the library, including the new state-of-the-art book sorting machine, for processing returns located in the staff area. As he saw the books being returned through pigeonholes by the borrowers and the computerized conveyor belt sorting them into the correct bin for reshelving, the sight made him laugh and prompted the telling of that story.<br /><br />Andrea wrote the book for his teacher while in the employ of Telkom, but the completed manuscript was taken from his room, which was located in a Bandung student accommodation community. Whoever took the manuscript knew enough to send it to a publisher and that’s how Andrea, an unhappy postal service worker who had studied economics in Europe and the UK, became the accidental author of the biggest selling novel in Indonesia’s history.<br /><br />He has since written seven more books. <br /><br />Fast forward to 2011 and Andrea was in Iowa, the US, where he did a reading of his short story, The Dry Season. He was approached by an independent literary agent, Kathleen Anderson. They talked, but for six months there was no news until an email arrived telling him that one of the best publishers in the US, Farrar, Straus and Giroux, had accepted his book. <br /><br />Then every week, more publishers said “yes” and now he has 24 contracts from the world’s leading publishers.<br /><br />Andrea worked with Angie Kilbane of the US on the English translations of Laskar Pelangi and its sequel Sang Pemimpi (The Dreamer). Translators from several other countries have visited his home village in Belitung to do research. <br /><br />“For a long time I wondered what was the key to the enormous success of my book,” Andrea said. <br /><br />“I think there’s no single right answer. Perhaps people are fed up with writing focused on urban issues or esca</span>

Selami ironisnya kehidupan mereka, kejujuran pemikiran mereka, indahnya petualangan mereka, dan temukan diri Anda tertawa, menangis, dan tersentuh saat membaca setiap lembarnya.
